[30;1m267 | [0m[35m=============[0m
[30;1m268 | [0m[35mDoing many small remote method calls in sequence has a fair amount of latency and overhead.[0m
[30;1m269 | [0m[35mPyro provides a means to gather all these small calls and submit it as a single 'batched call'.[0m
[30;1m270 | [0m[35mWhen the server processed them all, you get back all results at once.[0m
[30;1m271 | [0m[35mDepending on the size of the arguments, the network speed, and the amount of calls,[0m
[30;1m272 | [0m[35mdoing a batched call can be *much* faster than invoking every call by itself.[0m
[30;1m273 | [0m[35mNote that this feature is only available for calls on the same proxy object.[0m

[30;1m19 | [0m[35mObject discovery[0m
[30;1m20 | [0m[35m================[0m
[30;1m21 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m22 | [0m[35mTo be able to call methods on a Pyro object, you have to tell Pyro where it can find[0m
[30;1m23 | [0m[35mthe actual object. This is done by creating an appropriate URI, which contains amongst[0m
[30;1m24 | [0m[35mothers the object name and the location where it can be found.[0m

[30;1m133 | [0m[35mMultiple network interfaces[0m
[30;1m134 | [0m[35m===========================[0m
[30;1m135 | [0m[35mThis is a difficult subject but here are a few short notes about it.[0m
[30;1m136 | [0m[35m*At this time, Pyro doesn't support running on multiple network interfaces at the same time*.[0m
[30;1m137 | [0m[35mYou can bind a deamon on INADDR_ANY (0.0.0.0) though, including the name server.[0m
[30;1m138 | [0m[35mBut weird things happen with the URIs of objects published through these servers, because they[0m
[30;1m139 | [0m[35mwill point to 0.0.0.0 and your clients won't be able to connect to the actual objects.[0m
